<div id="review_601576501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601576501" />
    <a title="Breton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12771381-breton"><img alt="Breton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391229392p2/12771381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601576501?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Breton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Breton" href="/user/show/12771381-breton">Breton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553901238" href="/book/show/7421054-the-armageddon-rag">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601576501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12051675705918180940">...I'm still trying to figure out whether or not I liked this novel. <br/><br/>There's certainly a lot to be admired here. Martin's passion for music is made pretty clear quite early on, his grasp on theme is also pretty good, and for the most part I enjoyed the first nine-tenths of the novel. <br/><br/>The plot is slow moving, the characters don't particularly develop much, but the atmosphere is fairly interesting, and it was the atmosphere and the music that kept me reading (you could argue THOSE were the princip</span>
  <span id="freeText12051675705918180940" style="display:none">...I'm still trying to figure out whether or not I liked this novel. <br /><br />There's certainly a lot to be admired here. Martin's passion for music is made pretty clear quite early on, his grasp on theme is also pretty good, and for the most part I enjoyed the first nine-tenths of the novel. <br /><br />The plot is slow moving, the characters don't particularly develop much, but the atmosphere is fairly interesting, and it was the atmosphere and the music that kept me reading (you could argue THOSE were the principal characters). <br /><br />And Martin is well known (negatively or positively depending on who you ask) for his indulgence in description, his sometimes relentless hammering of fine details into the reader's head. I never had a problem with this in his ASOIAF books, even when he took his time to guide us through an entire lordly feast while describing every plate of food and every lord and their fascinating garments. But I did have a problem with it here--at times. <br /><br />One occasion that sticks in my memory is coincidentally a memory described by Sandy, in which he recalls a fairly shocking event in his life. Not only does it take about five or six pages to describe (at least it felt like that), but Martin repeats the word "faceless" over a dozen times in that sequence. <br /><br />While the plot is slow, it was usually interesting, and Sandy was always entertaining, but the end felt sort of...lacking. The last few pages almost felt like a frantic wrapping up of loose ends in a way that felt unrealistically positive considering where the story was headed. And one of the twists near the end could be seen coming from a mile away. <br /><br />I suppose I would give this novel two and a half stars if Goodreads would let me, but it doesn't, and I think three is a bit of a stretch, so I'll settle for two. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12051675705918180940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1185260685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185260685" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9338822-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336402386p2/9338822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185260685?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/9338822-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185260685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16594115869040378258">Like a lot of folks, I wasn't quite sure what I was reading when I started Armageddon Rag. I had just finished Fevre Dream by Martin, and the quicker pace of Fevre Dream through me off a bit to start since I started reading Armageddon Rag the same day that I finished Fevre Dream. <br/><br/>As I got deeper into Rag, I got accustomed to the pace. The story definitely took time to develop, and I grew impatient a few times. I had problems identifying with a lot of characters, but I'm chalking that up to me al</span>
  <span id="freeText16594115869040378258" style="display:none">Like a lot of folks, I wasn't quite sure what I was reading when I started Armageddon Rag. I had just finished Fevre Dream by Martin, and the quicker pace of Fevre Dream through me off a bit to start since I started reading Armageddon Rag the same day that I finished Fevre Dream. <br /><br />As I got deeper into Rag, I got accustomed to the pace. The story definitely took time to develop, and I grew impatient a few times. I had problems identifying with a lot of characters, but I'm chalking that up to me also not being a flower child (I was about 11 years old when this book was originally published). But Martin got me interested enough in Sandy to want to keep going. <br /><br />Sandy's weird visions of the past were a bit too long and scattered for me (maybe I am just impatient), but they were a great tool to give insight into Sandy. What I never quite understood was why Sandy was just a little bit more strong-willed than so many folks who fell under the spell so easily. Ananda definitely fooled him, but that was because he was thinking with different parts of his anatomy. But why was able to handle the pressure and keep his wits (relatively) about him when others couldn't? I never got that from the text. Was it just his natural ability, or his experiences, or both? Or something else?<br /><br />The end seemed very vacuous for a George RR Martin book. Maybe he hadn't developed his love for killing everyone yet in 1983, but I was really disappointed in the final chapter. <br /><br />All-in-all, I could have done without reading this, but I am kinda glad I did if just for the sake of getting insight into Martin's earlier stuff. I wouldn't tell someone not to read it, but I would say to be prepared for a bit if lugging through the heavy counter-culture to get to the meat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16594115869040378258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_718383424" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Isblue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1890483-isblue"><img alt="Isblue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231604841p2/1890483.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718383424?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isblue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isblue" href="/user/show/1890483-isblue">Isblue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1890483-isblue?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1890483-isblue?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1890483-isblue?shelf=2013">2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718383424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11499496970568614822">This is the first time I've read this book since it was released in paperback, the first time. The book is not science fiction and it's barely fantasy. There are definitely elements of the horror genre. I wouldn't call it a mystery or a thriller though it contains both elements. I think my favourite thing about this book is the descriptive language. You can almost see the dreams and visions he describes, and you will quail. Powerful words give the reader some of the best writing on rock music an</span>
  <span id="freeText11499496970568614822" style="display:none">This is the first time I've read this book since it was released in paperback, the first time. The book is not science fiction and it's barely fantasy. There are definitely elements of the horror genre. I wouldn't call it a mystery or a thriller though it contains both elements. I think my favourite thing about this book is the descriptive language. You can almost see the dreams and visions he describes, and you will quail. Powerful words give the reader some of the best writing on rock music and concerts I've read. I liked some of his characters, I hated others, just as a reader should. I liked the book a lot. <br /><br />I have to say I enjoyed the experience of reading this book a great deal more than I did twenty-eight years ago. I had not experienced life enough to see the dreams and hopes of a generation vanish, to see change actuallly happen as I watched, to see corruption grow and spread. Now I can relate more to Sandy and the despair he felt on the loss of his generation's dreams. I think every generation if not every individual has this moment. The moment you think how did we come to this, how did we let this happen? If that moment hasn't arrived yet, in time, it will. <br /><br />The book looks at how easy it is to fall in line and ignore your own concerns, how simple it is to look with suspicion and derision on those who are different from the herd you are a part of, and how common it is to seek out family in every kind of grouping.<br /><br />The Armageddon Rag is an excellent read. I'm really glad I finally read it again, and that I was more able to appreciate it this time around. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11499496970568614822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_320833454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/320833454" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5975160-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/320833454?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/5975160-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575129535" href="/book/show/13613086-the-armageddon-rag">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320833454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11663617696223896669">This hardback re-issue of George R.R. Martin's 1983 novel 'The Armageddon Rag' is strikingly eye-catching. The storyline is similarly grabbing. Compared to 'Fevre Dream' and 'A Song of Ice and Fire', this book's fantasy elements are very toned down. Instead, this book examines the power of rock music in our culture. Sandy Blair is a struggling writer/journalist hired to investigate the murder of a very rich rock promoter, most famous for making the Nazgul a world-renowned band.<br/><br/>The novel graduall</span>
  <span id="freeText11663617696223896669" style="display:none">This hardback re-issue of George R.R. Martin's 1983 novel 'The Armageddon Rag' is strikingly eye-catching. The storyline is similarly grabbing. Compared to 'Fevre Dream' and 'A Song of Ice and Fire', this book's fantasy elements are very toned down. Instead, this book examines the power of rock music in our culture. Sandy Blair is a struggling writer/journalist hired to investigate the murder of a very rich rock promoter, most famous for making the Nazgul a world-renowned band.<br /><br />The novel gradually progresses from a warm reminiscence of the 1960s to a dark, disturbing tale questioning modern day society. I was surprised and impressed by how angry Martin's writing was here; he writes with passion and fury, and in turn got my blood pumping, too. The characters are well drawn, as is to be expected from Martin.<br /><br />Why's it dropped down a star to 4, though? Well, there are a lot of dream sequences and prophesies, which I HATE! Unlike in 'ASOIAF', where Martin has perfected the craft of prophesisng events so that even I enjoy reading those dream-sequences, here they felt forced and distracting. Another critism is the ending: it seemed weak and rushed. When the rest of the story is so excellent,a weak ending is all the more disappointing.<br /><br />But don't let that put you off. The characters are vivid and multi-layered, the writing is loud and angry without losing any subtlety, and Martin constantly got me contemplating on the power of rock music. To end this review on a cliche: 'The Armageddon Rag' will rock your world! 4/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11663617696223896669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1829019008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1829019008" />
    <a title="Samuel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43839884-samuel"><img alt="Samuel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590248867p2/43839884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1829019008?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samuel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samuel" href="/user/show/43839884-samuel">Samuel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43839884-samuel?shelf=2016-books">2016-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1829019008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8944055200399418659">A heartfelt ode to the 1960s in the form of a mystery novel centring on a series of murders connected to a fictional Led Zeppelin-esque rock band. <br/><br/>Like “Dying of the Light”, you can feel Martin’s own experiences bleed through the text. His complex, shifting thoughts and attitudes towards the cultural shift in American society across the twentieth century are filtered through a novel that is in parts road trip, thriller, journalistic odyssey, supernatural horror, and song lyrics. It’s strikingly </span>
  <span id="freeText8944055200399418659" style="display:none">A heartfelt ode to the 1960s in the form of a mystery novel centring on a series of murders connected to a fictional Led Zeppelin-esque rock band. <br /><br />Like “Dying of the Light”, you can feel Martin’s own experiences bleed through the text. His complex, shifting thoughts and attitudes towards the cultural shift in American society across the twentieth century are filtered through a novel that is in parts road trip, thriller, journalistic odyssey, supernatural horror, and song lyrics. It’s strikingly earnest, clearly a novel from the heart, but the plot itself is compelling enough that it would have been a decent enough novel even without the intensely personal overtures. With those, however, the novel is legitimately one of Martin’s best works, and it saddens me to read that it was such a commercial dud at release. <br /><br />I was born decades after the setting of the novel, and my own personal enjoyment of the sorts of bands described in the text comes devoid of the cultural context they earned their popularity in, but the earnest humanism of the protagonist, so often an avatar for Martin, is far more compelling than any “mid-life crisis” style narrative, like the novel is on a superficial level, has any right to be, but Martin’s earnestness and skill in characterisation sees that the novel transcends its premise.<br /><br />It’s a delightfully unusual novel, bursting with heart, and displaying the skills in characterisation and deft handling of multiple genres that would eventually catapult Martin to legitimate celebrity. I give it four chords, and an encore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8944055200399418659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l9HcJvXEV2BQMwDQ226XjxZ5UgNRG98cKKXF8RYf15ghCddgLgLalG6SWqUyZecA08Z4lxD6V3z3+/382MXTaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">About George R.R. Martin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_111x148-e08b4682eea7088f8cdfd67c131d51cd.png);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">George R.R. Martin
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1258221545232883371">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br/><br/>Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood chil</span>
  <span id="freeText1258221545232883371" style="display:none">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br /><br />Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood children for pennies, dramatic readings included. Later he became a comic book fan and collector in high school, and began to write fiction for comic fanzines (amateur fan magazines). Martin's first professional sale was made in 1970 at age 21: "The Hero," sold to Galaxy, published in February, 1971 issue. Other sales followed. <br /><br />In 1970 Martin received a B.S. in Journalism from Northwestern University, Evanston, Illinois, graduating summa cum laude. He went on to complete a M.S. in Journalism in 1971, also from Northwestern. <br /><br />As a conscientious objector, Martin did alternative service 1972-1974 with VISTA, attached to Cook County Legal Assistance Foundation. He also directed chess tournaments for the Continental Chess Association from 1973-1976, and was a Journalism instructor at Clarke College, Dubuque, Iowa, from 1976-1978. He wrote part-time throughout the 1970s while working as a VISTA Volunteer, chess director, and teacher. <br /><br />In 1975 he married Gale Burnick. They divorced in 1979, with no children. Martin became a full-time writer in 1979. He was writer-in-residence at Clarke College from 1978-79. <br /><br />Moving on to Hollywood, Martin signed on as a story editor for Twilight Zone at CBS Television in 1986. In 1987 Martin became an Executive Story Consultant for Beauty and the Beast at CBS. In 1988 he became a Producer for Beauty and the Beast, then in 1989 moved up to Co-Supervising Producer. He was Executive Producer for Doorways, a pilot which he wrote for Columbia Pictures Television, which was filmed during 1992-93. <br /><br />Martin's present home is Santa Fe, New Mexico. He is a member of Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Writers of America (he was South-Central Regional Director 1977-1979, and Vice President 1996-1998), and of Writers' Guild of America, West. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/georgerrmartin">http://us.macmillan.com/author/george...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1258221545232883371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
